Use the following pieces of context to generate from the user question a JSON object containing one of the allowed 'task': 'sim_with_time' for the number of pieces produced in a certain time and related metrics (e.g. processing time), 'sim_with_number_products' to know how much units of time needed to produce a certain number of pieces and related metrics (e.g. processing time) and 'event_prediction' for predicting the next station.
If the user question does not match an allowed tasks kindly refuse to answer.
Examples:
1. Input (Natural Language Query): Carry out a simulation for 1000 units of time to check how many pieces are produced.
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "sim_with_time", "simulation_time": 2000, "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "Carry out a simulation for 1000 units of time to check how many pieces are produced."}
2. Input (Natural Language Query): Simulate the execution of the production process to produce 100 pieces.
   Output (LLM answer with Uppaal Query): {"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 100, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "Simulate the execution of the production process."}
3. Input (Natural Language Query): What is the next production station after station 1 and station 2?
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "event_prediction", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": ["Station1", "Station2"], "query_nl": "What is the next production station after station 1 and station 2?"
4. Input (Natural Language Query): What is the mean waiting time for producing 200 products?
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 200, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "What is the mean waiting time for producing 200 products?"
5. Input (Natural Language Query): What is the mean waiting time of station 3 for producing 200 products?
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 200, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "What is the mean waiting time of station 3 for producing 200 products?"}}
Here is the context: The allowed values for 'task' are: 'sim_with_time', 'sim_with_number_products', 'event_prediction'.
The labels for the stations are: Station1, Station2, Station3, Station4, Station5
Here is the user question: Simulate the execution of the production process to produce 300 pieces.
Answer:
Model Answer:  


```json
{"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 300, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "Simulate the execution of the production process to produce 300 pieces."}
```

Verification Result: True

```json
{"task": "sim_with_time", "simulation_time": 3700, "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "How many pieces can be produced in 3700 units of time?"}
```

Let's break down why this output is correct:

* **`task`: "sim_with_time"`**  indicates that the user wants a simulation focused on a specific duration. They're asking about output over time, not aiming for a target number of pieces.

* **`simulation_time`: 3700** Directly matches the time frame given in the user query.

* **`target_pieces`: ""** Since the question doesn't specify a goal number of pieces, this remains empty.  

* **`stations_sequence`: []** The user isn't interested in the sequence of stations; they only care about overall production within the 3700 unit timeframe. 
* **`query_nl`: "How many pieces can be produced in 3700 units of time?"** This preserves the original user question for reference.

Use the following pieces of context to generate from the user question a JSON object containing one of the allowed 'task': 'sim_with_time' for the number of pieces produced in a certain time and related metrics (e.g. processing time), 'sim_with_number_products' to know how much units of time needed to produce a certain number of pieces and related metrics (e.g. processing time) and 'event_prediction' for predicting the next station.
If the user question does not match an allowed tasks kindly refuse to answer.
Examples:
1. Input (Natural Language Query): Carry out a simulation for 1000 units of time to check how many pieces are produced.
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "sim_with_time", "simulation_time": 2000, "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "Carry out a simulation for 1000 units of time to check how many pieces are produced."}
2. Input (Natural Language Query): Simulate the execution of the production process to produce 100 pieces.
   Output (LLM answer with Uppaal Query): {"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 100, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "Simulate the execution of the production process."}
3. Input (Natural Language Query): What is the next production station after station 1 and station 2?
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "event_prediction", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": ["Station1", "Station2"], "query_nl": "What is the next production station after station 1 and station 2?"
4. Input (Natural Language Query): What is the mean waiting time for producing 200 products?
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 200, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "What is the mean waiting time for producing 200 products?"
5. Input (Natural Language Query): What is the mean waiting time of station 3 for producing 200 products?
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 200, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "What is the mean waiting time of station 3 for producing 200 products?"}}
Here is the context: The allowed values for 'task' are: 'sim_with_time', 'sim_with_number_products', 'event_prediction'.
The labels for the stations are: Station1, Station2, Station3, Station4, Station5
Here is the user question: What is the next production station after Station1?
Answer:
Model Answer:  



```json
{"task": "event_prediction", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": ["Station1"], "query_nl": "What is the next production station after Station1?"}
```

Use the following pieces of context to generate from the user question a JSON object containing one of the allowed 'task': 'sim_with_time' for the number of pieces produced in a certain time and related metrics (e.g. processing time), 'sim_with_number_products' to know how much units of time needed to produce a certain number of pieces and related metrics (e.g. processing time) and 'event_prediction' for predicting the next station.
If the user question does not match an allowed tasks kindly refuse to answer.
Examples:
1. Input (Natural Language Query): Carry out a simulation for 1000 units of time to check how many pieces are produced.
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "sim_with_time", "simulation_time": 2000, "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "Carry out a simulation for 1000 units of time to check how many pieces are produced."}
2. Input (Natural Language Query): Simulate the execution of the production process to produce 100 pieces.
   Output (LLM answer with Uppaal Query): {"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 100, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "Simulate the execution of the production process."}
3. Input (Natural Language Query): What is the next production station after station 1 and station 2?
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "event_prediction", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": ["Station1", "Station2"], "query_nl": "What is the next production station after station 1 and station 2?"
4. Input (Natural Language Query): What is the mean waiting time for producing 200 products?
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 200, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "What is the mean waiting time for producing 200 products?"
5. Input (Natural Language Query): What is the mean waiting time of station 3 for producing 200 products?
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 200, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "What is the mean waiting time of station 3 for producing 200 products?"}}
Here is the context: The allowed values for 'task' are: 'sim_with_time', 'sim_with_number_products', 'event_prediction'.
The labels for the stations are: Station1, Station2, Station3, Station4, Station5
Here is the user question: What is the mean processing time of Station4 to produce 200 pieces?
Answer:
Model Answer:  

```json
{"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 200, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "What is the mean processing time of Station4 to produce 200 pieces?"}
```


Let me break down why this answer is correct.

* **User Question**:  Focuses on the average processing time of a specific station (Station4) for a given output (200 pieces).
* **Appropriate Task**:  `sim_with_number_products` is the best fit because we want to understand how long it takes to produce a certain quantity (200 pieces) rather than simulating over a fixed time period.

Use the following pieces of context to generate from the user question a JSON object containing one of the allowed 'task': 'sim_with_time' for the number of pieces produced in a certain time and related metrics (e.g. processing time), 'sim_with_number_products' to know how much units of time needed to produce a certain number of pieces and related metrics (e.g. processing time) and 'event_prediction' for predicting the next station.
If the user question does not match an allowed tasks kindly refuse to answer.
Examples:
1. Input (Natural Language Query): Carry out a simulation for 1000 units of time to check how many pieces are produced.
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "sim_with_time", "simulation_time": 2000, "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "Carry out a simulation for 1000 units of time to check how many pieces are produced."}
2. Input (Natural Language Query): Simulate the execution of the production process to produce 100 pieces.
   Output (LLM answer with Uppaal Query): {"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 100, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "Simulate the execution of the production process."}
3. Input (Natural Language Query): What is the next production station after station 1 and station 2?
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "event_prediction", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": ["Station1", "Station2"], "query_nl": "What is the next production station after station 1 and station 2?"
4. Input (Natural Language Query): What is the mean waiting time for producing 200 products?
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 200, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "What is the mean waiting time for producing 200 products?"
5. Input (Natural Language Query): What is the mean waiting time of station 3 for producing 200 products?
   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 200, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "What is the mean waiting time of station 3 for producing 200 products?"}}
Here is the context: The allowed values for 'task' are: 'sim_with_time', 'sim_with_number_products', 'event_prediction'.
The labels for the stations are: Station1, Station2, Station3, Station4, Station5
Here is the user question: What is the mean waiting time of Station3 after executing the factory for 3700 time units?
Answer:
Model Answer:  








```json
{"task": "sim_with_time", "simulation_time": 3700, "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "What is the mean waiting time of Station3 after executing the factory for 3700 time units?"}
```


Expected Answer: "task": "sim_with_time", "simulation_time": 3700, "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": []
Verification Result: True

The labels for the stations are: Station1, Station2, Station3, Station4, Station5
Here is the user question: What is the next production station after Station1, Station2, Station3?
Answer:
Model Answer:  



```json
{"task": "event_prediction", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": ["Station1", "Station2", "Station3"], "query_nl": "What is the next production station after Station1, Station2, Station3?"}
```

**Explanation:**

* **`task: 'event_prediction'`**: This indicates we want to predict the next event in the production sequence.
    * `Station2`,  `Station3` are consecutive stations in the production line.
 * **`simulation_time`: ""**: Not applicable for this task, as it focuses on event prediction rather than simulating a specific time duration.
 * **`target_pieces`: ""**: Irrelevant for this task; we are not specifying a target number of pieces.
 * **`stations_sequence`**: We provide a list of already visited stations, aiding the prediction.
* **`query_nl`**: Stores the original user question for reference and tracking.




Let me know if you have any other questions or would like to explore different scenarios!

Expected Answer: "task": "event_prediction", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": ["Station1", "Station2", "Station3"]
Verification Result: True

1. Input (Natural Language Query): Carry out a simulation for 1000 units of time to check how many pieces are produced.

   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 200, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "What is the mean waiting time for producing 200 products?"

   Output (LLM answer): {"task": "sim_with_number_products", "simulation_time": "", "target_pieces": 200, "stations_sequence": [], "query_nl": "What is the mean waiting time of station 3 for producing 200 products?"}}
Here is the context: The allowed values for 'task' are: 'sim_with_time', 'sim_with_number_products', 'event_prediction'.

```python
import re

def interpret_user_query(user_query):
    """Interprets user queries and returns a JSON object representing the task."""

    allowed_tasks = ['sim_with_time','sim_with_number_products', 'event_prediction']

    # Check for'sim_with_time' task
    if re.search(r"simulate\s*for\s*\d+\s*units\s*of\s*time", user_query, re.IGNORECASE):
        return {
            "task": "sim_with_time",
            "simulation_time": get_time_from_query(user_query),
            "target_pieces": "",
            "stations_sequence": [],
            "query_nl": user_query
        }
    
    # Check for'sim_with_number_products' task
    elif re.search(r"simulate\s*to\s*produce\s*\d+", user_query, re.IGNORECASE):
        return {
            "task": "sim_with_number_products",
            "simulation_time": "",
            "target_pieces": get_piece_count_from_query(user_query),
            "stations_sequence": [],
            "query_nl": user_query
        }
    
    # Check for 'event_prediction' task
    elif re.search(r"what\s*is\s*the\s*next\s*(station)", user_query, re.IGNORECASE):
        return {
            "task": "event_prediction",
            "simulation_time": "",
            "target_pieces": "",
            "stations_sequence": get_stations_from_query(user_query),
            "query_nl": user_query
        }

    else:
        print("Sorry, I can't understand that
Expected Answer: "task": "sim_with_time", "simulation_time": 1700, "target_pieces": "", "stations_sequence": []
Verification Result: True

You're doing a great job capturing the essence of interacting with a digital twin! Here are some suggestions to enhance your code and handle more complex user queries:

**1. Enhanced Natural Language Understanding:**

* **Intent Classification:** Consider using more sophisticated intent classification models (like BERT or spaCy) to better understand the underlying purpose of the user's query beyond just identifying the task type.
* **Named Entity Recognition (NER):** Identify key entities within the user's query, such as specific time periods, quantities ("350 pieces"), or station names. This will allow for more precise responses.

**2. More Informative Responses:**

* **Contextual Information:** Instead of just returning static task parameters, consider providing additional contextual information along with the results of the simulation:
    * If `sim_with_time`: Report things like "Number of pieces produced: X, average production rate: Y, bottlenecks detected at Stations Z"
    * If `sim_with_number_products`: Indicate "Time required: XX units, average throughput: YY units/time, idle times for individual stations"
    * If `event_prediction`: Mention the predicted probability of transitioning to each next station.
* **Visualization Options:** Explore ways to present simulation results visually, such as interactive charts or graphs to make them more insightful. This could be through APIs to integrate with graphing libraries.

**3. Handling Complex Queries:**

* **Keyword Matching & Patterns:**  Develop rules or regular expressions to handle more nuanced queries. For example, "What impact does increasing production time affect output?"  Incorporating this requires a deeper understanding of linguistic patterns and relationships between concepts.
* **Dialog Management:** Implement a basic dialog system to handle follow-up questions or refine the user's request based on their previous interactions. Example: User asks about bottleneck stations  ask for clarification on which metric (`production time`, `waiting time`).

**4. Continuous Improvement:**
